the runtime behavior for LangGraph applications.\n\n    ## Overview\n\n    Pregel combines [**actors**](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Actor_model)\n    and **channels** into a single application.\n    **Actors** read data from channels and write data to channels.\n    Pregel organizes the execution of the application into multiple steps,\n    following the **Pregel Algorithm**/**Bulk Synchronous Parallel** model.\n\n    Each step consists of three phases:\n\n    - **Plan**: Determine which **actors** to execute in this step. For example,\n        in the first step, select the **actors** that subscribe to the special\n        **input** channels; in subsequent steps,\n        select the **actors** that subscribe to channels updated in the previous step.\n    - **Execution**: Execute all selected **actors** in parallel,\n        until all complete, or one fails, or a timeout is reached. During this\n        phase, channel updates are invisible to actors until the next step.\n    - **Update**: Update the channels with the values written by the **actors**\n        in this step.\n\n    Repeat until no **actors** are selected for execution, or a maximum number of\n    steps is reached.\n\n    ## Actors\n\n    An **actor** is a `PregelNode`.\n    It subscribes to channels, reads data from them, and writes data to them.\n    It can be thought of as an **actor** in the Pregel algorithm.\n    `PregelNodes` implement LangChain's\n    Runnable interface.\n\n    ## Channels\n\n    Channels are used to communicate between actors (`PregelNodes`).\n    Each channel has a value type, an update type, and an update function – which\n    takes a sequence of updates and\n    modifies the stored value. Channels can be used to send data from one chain to\n    another, or to send data from a chain to itself in a future step. LangGraph\n    provides a number of built-in channels:\n\n    ### Basic channels: LastValue and Topic\n\n    - `LastValue`: The default channel, stores the last value sent to the channel,\n       useful for input and output values, or for sending data from one step to the next\n    - `Topic`: A configurable PubSub Topic, useful for sending multiple values\n       between *actors*, or for accumulating output. Can be configured to deduplicate\n       values, and/or to accumulate values over the course of multiple steps.\n\n    ### Advanced channels: Context and BinaryOperatorAggregate\n\n    - `Context`: exposes the value of a context manager, managing its lifecycle.\n        Useful for accessing external resources that require setup and/or teardown. e.g.\n        `client = Context(httpx.Client)`\n    - `BinaryOperatorAggregate`: stores a persistent value, updated by applying\n        a binary operator to the current value and each update\n        sent to the channel, useful for computing aggregates over multiple steps. e.g.\n        `total = BinaryOperatorAggregate(int, operator.add)`\n\n    ## Examples\n\n    Most users will interact with Pregel via a\n    [StateGraph (Graph API)][langgraph.graph.StateGraph] or via an\n    [entrypoint (Functional API)][langgraph.func.entrypoint].\n\n    However, for **advanced** use cases, Pregel can be used directly. If you're\n    not sure whether you need to use Pregel directly, then the answer is probably no\n    - you should use the Graph API or Functional API instead. These are higher-level\n    interfaces that will compile down to Pregel under the hood.\n\n    Here are some examples to give you a sense of how it works:\n\n    Example: Single node application\n        ```python\n        from langgraph.channels import EphemeralValue\n        from langgraph.pregel import Pregel, NodeBuilder\n\n        node1 = (\n            NodeBuilder().subscribe_only(\"a\")\n            .do(lambda x: x + x)\n            .write_to(\"b\")\n        )\n\n        app = Pregel(\n            nodes={\"node1\": node1},\n            channels={\n                \"a\": EphemeralValue(str),\n                \"b\": EphemeralValue(str),\n            },\n            input_channels=[\"a\"],\n            output_channels=[\"b\"],\n        )\n\n        app.invoke({\"a\": \"foo\"})\n        ```\n\n        ```con\n        {'b': 'foofoo'}\n        ```\n\n    Example: Using multiple nodes and multiple output channels\n        ```python\n        from langgraph.channels import LastValue, EphemeralValue\n        from langgraph.pregel import Pregel, NodeBuilder\n\n        node1 = (\n            NodeBuilder().subscribe_only(\"a\")\n            .do(lambda x: x + x)\n            .write_to(\"b\")\n        )\n\n        node2 = (\n            NodeBuilder().subscribe_to(\"b\")\n            .do(lambda x: x[\"b\"] + x[\"b\"])\n            .write_to(\"c\")\n        )\n\n\n        app = Pregel(\n            nodes={\"node1\": node1, \"node2\": node2},\n            channels={\n                \"a\": EphemeralValue(str),\n                \"b\": LastValue(str),\n                \"c\": EphemeralValue(str),\n            },\n            input_channels=[\"a\"],\n            output_channels=[\"b\", \"c\"],\n        )\n\n        app.invoke({\"a\": \"foo\"})\n        ```\n\n        ```con\n        {'b': 'foofoo', 'c': 'foofoofoofoo'}\n        ```\n\n    Example: Using a Topic channel\n        ```python\n        from langgraph.channels import LastValue, EphemeralValue, Topic\n        from langgraph.pregel import Pregel, NodeBuilder\n\n        node1 = (\n            NodeBuilder().subscribe_only(\"a\")\n            .do(lambda x: x + x)\n            .write_to(\"b\", \"c\")\n        )\n\n        node2 = (\n            NodeBuilder().subscribe_only(\"b\")\n            .do(lambda x: x + x)\n            .write_to(\"c\")\n        )\n\n\n        app = Pregel(\n            nodes={\"node1\": node1, \"node2\": node2},\n            channels={\n                \"a\": EphemeralValue(str),\n                \"b\": EphemeralValue(str),\n                \"c\": Topic(str, accumulate=True),\n            },\n            input_channels=[\"a\"],\n            output_channels=[\"c\"],\n        )\n\n        app.invoke({\"a\": \"foo\"})\n        ```\n\n        ```pycon\n BinaryOperatorAggregate\n        from langgraph.pregel import Pregel, NodeBuilder\n\n\n        node1 = (\n            NodeBuilder().subscribe_only(\"a\")\n            .do(lambda x: x + x)\n            .write_to(\"b\", \"c\")\n        )\n\n        node2 = (\n            NodeBuilder().subscribe_only(\"b\")\n            .do(lambda x: x + x)\n            .write_to(\"c\")\n        )\n\n\n        def reducer(current, update):\n            if current:\n                return current + \" | \" + update\n            else:\n                return update\n\n\n        app = Pregel(\n            nodes={\"node1\": node1, \"node2\": node2},\n            channels={\n                \"a\": EphemeralValue(str),\n                \"b\": EphemeralValue(str),\n                \"c\": BinaryOperatorAggregate(str, operator=reducer),\n            },\n            input_channels=[\"a\"],\n            output_channels=[\"c\"],\n        )\n\n        app.invoke({\"a\": \"foo\"})\n        ```\n\n        ```con\n        {'c': 'foofoo | foofoofoofoo'}\n        ```\n\n    Example: Introducing a cycle\n        This example demonstrates how to introduce a cycle in the graph, by having\n EphemeralValue\n        from langgraph.pregel import Pregel, NodeBuilder, ChannelWriteEntry\n\n        example_node = (\n            NodeBuilder()\n            .subscribe_only(\"value\")\n example_node},\n            channels={\n                \"value\": EphemeralValue(str),\n            },\n            input_channels=[\"value\"],\n            output_channels=[\"value\"],\n Fresh subagent per task with dual review.\"\n\n## The Process\n\n### Setup\n1. Read the full plan and extract all tasks\n2. Create a TodoWrite with all tasks for tracking\n3. Verify an approved spec exists before starting\n\n### Per Task\n\n```\nDispatch implementer → spec reviewer → code quality reviewer → mark complete\n```\n\n1. **Dispatch implementer** with precise context (see \"Implementer Prompt\")\n2. **Wait for result** — analyze the returned status\n3. **Dispatch spec reviewer** (only after DONE)\n4. **If spec compliance approved:** dispatch code quality reviewer\n5. **If code quality approved:** mark task complete, advance\n6. **If any review fails:** fix and re-dispatch — never advance with unresolved issues\n\n### After All Tasks\n- Dispatch final code review\n- Use `finishing-a-branch` to complete the branch\n\n## Model Selection by Task\n\n| Task Type | Model |\n|-----------|-------|\n| Mechanical (1-2 files, clear spec) | haiku (cheaper) |\n| Integration/judgment calls | sonnet (standard) |\n| Architecture/design/review | opus (most capable) |\n\n## Implementer Statuses\n\n### DONE\nImplementation complete. Proceed to spec compliance review.\n\n### DONE_WITH_CONCERNS\nRead the concerns, assess:\n- Blocking for spec? → Fix before proceeding\n- Quality improvements? → Let code quality reviewer assess\n\n### NEEDS_CONTEXT\nProvide the specific requested context and re-dispatch. Common contexts:\n```\n\"Need the content of file X\" → Read and include in prompt\n\"Don't know how endpoint Y works\" → Include API contract\n\"What pattern to use for Z?\" → Include a codebase example\n```\n\n### BLOCKED\nAssess root cause before retrying:\n- Unimplemented dependency → Implement the dependency first\n- Design conflict → Escalate to user\n- Environment bug → Use `systematic-debugging`\n\n## Implementer Prompt\n\n```markdown\nYou are an engineer implementing Task N of the plan.\n\n**Task:** <task title>\n\n**Spec context:**\n<relevant spec section>\n\n**Plan context:**\n<full task with steps and code>\n\n**Files to create/modify:**\n<exact file list>\n\n**Project conventions:**\n- Backend: Django 5.2 + DRF, pytest + factory_boy, pattern Model→Serializer→Service→View\n- Frontend: React 18 + TypeScript strict, TanStack Query, MUI v5\n- Celery: bind=True, max_retries=3, transaction.on_commit() to dispatch tasks\n- Commits: feat(<app>): description / fix(<app>): description / test(<app>): description\n\n**TDD mandatory:**\n1. Write a failing test\n2. Confirm it fails for the right reason\n3. Implement minimal code\n4. Confirm it passes\n5. Commit\n\n**Return one of:**\n- DONE: implementation complete, all tests passing\n- DONE_WITH_CONCERNS: complete but with specific concerns [list them]\n- NEEDS_CONTEXT: needs specific context [list what's needed]\n- BLOCKED: blocked by [specific cause]\n```\n\n## Spec Reviewer Prompt\n\n```markdown\nYou are a reviewer verifying the implementation matches the spec.\n\n**Spec:** <relevant spec content>\n**Task implemented:** <description>\n**Implemented code:** <diff or modified files>\n\nVerify:\n1. All spec acceptance scenarios are addressed?\n2. API interfaces are correct (endpoints, payloads, status codes)?\n3. Models/fields match the spec?\n4. Error handling behavior is correct?\n5. Tests cover the spec scenarios?\n\nReturn: APPROVED or ISSUES_FOUND with specific list of violations.\n```\n\n## Code Quality Reviewer Prompt\n\n```markdown\nYou are a code quality reviewer.\n\n**Implemented code:** <diff or files>\n**Project context:** Django 5.2 + React 18 + TypeScript strict\n\nVerify:\n1. No Production Code Without a Failing Test First\n\nWrite code before the test? **Delete it. Start over.**\n\nNo exceptions:\n- Don't keep it as \"reference\"\n- Don't \"adapt\" it while writing tests\n- Don't look at it\n- Delete means delete\n\n### 2. No Implementation Without a Design First\n\nBefore any creative work - creating features, building components, adding functionality:\n1. Explore the idea through questions\n2. Present 2-3 approaches with trade-offs\n3. Validate design in sections (200-300 words each)\n4. Document the validated design\n\n### 3. No Completion Without Verification\n\n\"It works\" requires proof:\n- Tests pass (watched them fail first)\n- Manual verification of behavior\n- Edge cases covered\n- No regressions\n\n## Red-Green-Refactor Cycle\n\n```\nRED: Write failing test\n  ↓ Verify it fails for the right reason\nGREEN: Write minimal code to pass\n  ↓ Verify all tests pass\nREFACTOR: Clean up\n  ↓ Stay green\nREPEAT\n```\n\n## Common Rationalizations (And Why They're Wrong)\n\n| Excuse | Reality |\n|--------|---------|\n| \"Too simple to test\" | Simple code breaks. Test takes 30 seconds. |\n| \"I'll test after\" | Tests passing immediately prove nothing. |\n| \"Already manually tested\" | Ad-hoc ≠ systematic. No record, can't re-run. |\n| \"Deleting X hours is wasteful\" | Sunk cost fallacy. Keeping unverified code is debt. |\n| \"Need to explore first\" | Fine. Throw away exploration, start with TDD. |\n| \"TDD will slow me down\" | TDD faster than debugging. |\n| \"Tests after achieve same goals\" | Tests-after = \"what does this do?\" Tests-first = \"what should this do?\" |\n| \"Keep as reference, write tests first\" | You'll adapt it. That's testing after. Delete means delete. |\n| \"Test hard = design unclear\" | Listen to test. Hard to test = hard to use. |\n| \"Manual test faster\" | Manual doesn't prove edge cases. You'll re-test every change. |\n| \"Existing code has no tests\" | You're improving it. Add tests for existing code. |\n\n## Red Flags - STOP and Start Over\n\nIf you catch yourself:\n- Writing code before test\n- Test passes immediately (didn't watch it fail)\n- Rationalizing \"just this once\"\n- Saying \"I already manually tested it\"\n- Thinking \"it's about spirit not ritual\"\n- Saying \"this is different because...\"\n- Keeping code as \"reference\" while writing tests\n- Saying \"tests after achieve the same purpose\"\n\n**All of these mean: Delete code. Start over with TDD.**\n\n## Bite-Sized Task Granularity\n\nEach task should be 2-5 minutes:\n- \"Write the failing test\" - one step\n- \"Run it to make sure it fails\" - one step\n- \"Implement the minimal code\" - one step\n- \"Run tests and verify pass\" - one step\n- \"Commit\" - one step\n\n## Two-Stage Review Pattern\n\nAfter each task:\n\n**Stage 1: Spec Compliance Review**\n- Does implementation match the spec exactly?\n- Nothing missing from requirements?\n- Nothing extra that wasn't requested?\n\n**Stage 2: Code Quality Review**\n- Clean code principles followed?\n- Proper error handling?\n- Test coverage adequate?\n- No obvious issues?\n\nBoth stages must pass before moving to next task.\n\n## Subagent Advantages\n\nUsing fresh subagents per task provides:\n- **Clean context** - No pollution from previous work\n- **Focused attention** - Single task, single responsibility\n- **Quality gates** - Review checkpoints catch issues early\n- **Parallel safety** - Subagents don't interfere with each other\n\n## Integration Points\n\n| When | Skill/Agent |\n|------|-------------|\n| Starting new feature | brainstorming → writing-plans |\n| Implementing plan | subagent-driven-development |\n| Debugging issues | systematic-debugging |\n| Before declaring done | verification-before-completion |\n| Creating isolated workspace | using-git-worktrees |","is_error":false}]},"uuid":"6bc56b0e-b1f1-4ca5-b45d-2cbfe827d945","timestamp":"2026-03-20T13:40:06.681Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"6d3d6f8d-ef4f-479e-ae70-7b372152ac6f","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir","sessionId":"0c5a9bfa-6816-42b1-a97d-37ae7dad26c5","version":"2.1.80","gitBranch":"feat/remaining-6-fixes","slug":"mighty-wondering-giraffe"}

task_id: Unique identifier or name\n          - description: What needs to be implemented\n          - spec: The detailed specification/requirements\n          - acceptance_criteria: How to verify the task is complete\n          - files: Files likely to be created or modified\n          - dependencies: Any tasks this depends on (if applicable)\n\n          Return the tasks as a JSON array that can be iterated.\n          Order tasks by dependencies (independent tasks first, dependent tasks later).\n\n          IMPORTANT: Preserve ALL spec details - they are critical for review.\n        output: \"tasks\"\n        parse_json: true\n        timeout: 180\n\n      - id: \"validate-tasks\"\n        agent: \"foundation:zen-architect\"\n        mode: \"ANALYZE\"\n        prompt: |\n          Validate the extracted tasks before execution begins.\n\n          Tasks: {{tasks}}\n          Original plan: {{plan_path}}\n\n          Check:\n          1. Are there any tasks with unclear or missing specifications?\n          4. Do not consider other tasks.\n\n          TASK TO IMPLEMENT:\n          {{current_task}}\n\n          IMPLEMENTATION REQUIREMENTS:\n          \n          1. FOLLOW TDD (Test-Driven Development):\n             - Write failing tests FIRST based on the spec\n             - Implement code to make tests pass\n             - Refactor if needed while keeping tests green\n          \n          2. FOLLOW THE SPEC EXACTLY:\n             - Implement exactly what the spec says\n             - Do not add features not in the spec\n             - Do not skip any spec requirements\n             - Match the acceptance criteria precisely\n          \n          3. DOCUMENT YOUR WORK:\n             - List all files created/modified\n             - Note any important implementation decisions\n             - Record test coverage for this task\n          \n          4. VERIFY BEFORE COMPLETING:\n             - Run the tests you wrote\n             - Confirm they pass\n             - Check acceptance criteria are met\n\n          OUTPUT FORMAT:\n          Return your implementation results including:\n          - task_id: Which task was implemented\n          - files_changed: [list of files created/modified]\n          - tests_written: [list of test files/functions]\n          - test_results: pass/fail with details\n          - implementation_notes: Key decisions or notes\n          - spec_coverage: How each spec requirement was addressed\n        collect: \"task_implementations\"\n        timeout: 900  # 15 minutes per task\n\n      # -----------------------------------------------------------------------\n      # Step 3: Spec Compliance Review (Fresh Agent Per Task)\n      # -----------------------------------------------------------------------\n      - id: \"spec-compliance-review\"\n        foreach: \"{{task_implementations}}\"\n        as: \"implementation\"\n        agent: \"foundation:zen-architect\"\n        mode: \"REVIEW\"\n        prompt: |\n          SPEC COMPLIANCE REVIEW\n          ======================\n          Review Stage 1 of 2: Verify implementation matches specification EXACTLY.\n\n          IMPLEMENTATION TO REVIEW:\n          {{implementation}}\n\n          ORIGINAL TASKS (for spec reference):\n          {{tasks}}\n\n          YOUR MISSION:\n          Verify that the implementation matches the specification EXACTLY.\n          This is a STRICT compliance check - no deviations allowed.\n\n          REVIEW CHECKLIST:\n          1. [ ] Clean code principles followed\n          2. [ ] Proper naming conventions\n          3. [ ] No code duplication (DRY)\n          4. [ ] Appropriate abstraction levels\n          5. [ ] Error handling is robust\n          6. [ ] Tests are meaningful (not just coverage padding)\n          7. [ ] Code is maintainable and readable\n          8. [ ] No obvious performance issues\n          9. {"parentUuid":"8b9d328d-f9cf-43f5-9a46-26c153542fed","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"f78873c7-b11a-48ac-8895-44a9f886f328","agentId":"a324079de037abd7c","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_016fNHJo61RkGDpwfX5MLMsY","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# Architecture\n     2→\n     3→Wazir is a host-native engineering OS kit. The host environment (Claude, Codex, Gemini, Cursor) remains the execution container. Wazir supplies the operating model, guardrails, and artifact contracts.\n     4→\n     5→## Core components\n     6→\n     7→| Component | Purpose |\n     8→|-----------|---------|\n     9→| Roles | Canonical contracts defining what each agent role does and produces |\n    10→| Workflows | Phase entrypoints that sequence roles through delivery |\n    11→| Skills | Reusable procedures (wz:tdd, wz:debugging, wz:verification, wz:brainstorming) |\n    12→| Hooks | Guardrails enforcing protected paths, loop caps, and capture routing |\n    13→| Expertise | 315 curated knowledge modules composed into agent prompts |\n    14→| Templates | Artifact templates for phase outputs and handoff |\n    15→| Schemas | Validation schemas for manifest, hooks, artifacts, and exports |\n    16→| Exports | Generated host packages tailored per supported host |\n    17→| Tooling | CLI for validation, indexing, recall, capture, and status |\n    18→\n    19→## Design influences\n    20→\n    21→| Source | What Wazir keeps |\n    22→|--------|----------------------|\n    23→| Wazir skill system | Disciplined workflows, TDD, verification, review rigor, skill ergonomics |\n    24→| Spec-Kit | Spec-first development, explicit artifacts, approval gates |\n    25→| Oh My Claude | Host-native prompt structure and operator ergonomics |\n    26→| autoresearch | Research loops, experiment tracking, self-improvement discipline |\n    27→\n    28→## Context and indexing\n    29→\n    30→Wazir ships a built-in local index and recall surface that reduces context window consumption by 60-80% on exploration-heavy phases.\n    31→\n    32→### Context tiers\n    33→\n    34→| Tier | Token budget | Content | When to use |\n    35→|------|-------------|---------|-------------|\n    36→| L0 | ~100 tokens | One-line identifier (name, kind, language, line range) | Inventory scans, deciding what to load |\n    37→| L1 | ~500-2k tokens | Structural summary (signature, fields, purpose, dependencies) | Understanding shape without full source |\n    38→| L2 | Full content | Exact line-bounded source slice | Implementation, debugging, code review |\n    39→\n    40→### Role-specific recall defaults\n    41→\n    42→Roles are assigned default tiers based on their information needs:\n    43→\n    44→- **Exploration roles** (clarifier, researcher, specifier, content-author, designer, planner) default to L1 -- they need to understand structure across many files without reading every line\n    45→- **Implementation roles** (executor, verifier) default to direct read (L2) -- they need exact source for code changes and verification\n    46→- **Review role** (reviewer) starts at L1 as a triage pass, escalating to direct read only for logic errors, security concerns, or ambiguous summaries\n    47→- **Learning role** (learner) defaults to L0 -- it needs only inventory-level context to identify what changed\n    48→\n    49→Every role includes a fallback chain: if the preferred tier fails (no index, no summaries), the role falls back to direct file reads. The system degrades gracefully -- no wasted tokens on failed index operations.\n    50→\n    51→### Capture routing\n    52→\n    53→Large tool output is routed to run-local files via `wazir capture route` and `wazir capture output`, keeping the context window lean. The agent receives a file path reference (~50 tokens) instead of the full output.\n    54→\n    55→### Pipeline integration points\n    56→\n    57→The index and recall surface integrates with the pipeline at five points:\n    58→\n    59→1. **Session start** -- the bootstrap hook runs `index refresh` (or `build` for first run) to ensure the index is current\n    60→2. **Scan project** -- the `scan-project` skill runs `index stats` to report index health in the project profile\n    61→3. **Debugging** -- the `wz:debugging` OBSERVE phase uses `index search-symbols` and `recall --tier L1` for symbol-first exploration\n    62→4. **Execute** -- the executor uses `recall file` and `recall symbol` for targeted source reads\n    63→5. **Verify** -- the verifier uses direct reads for full validation\n    64→\n    65→### Measuring savings\n    66→\n    67→`wazir capture usage` generates a per-run token savings report showing capture routing statistics and context window savings. This provides concrete evidence of token reduction per session.\n    68→\n    69→The context-mode integration remains an optional adapter -- off by default, never required for core install, build, or test paths.\n    70→\n    71→See [Indexing and Recall](indexing-and-recall.md) for full command details and extractor documentation.\n    72→\n    73→## Design Phase\n    74→\n    75→The design phase runs after specification and before planning. The `designer` role uses open-pencil MCP tools to produce visual designs from the approved spec. Outputs include a `.fig` design file, exported Tailwind JSX/HTML+CSS scaffolds, design tokens JSON, and screenshot PNGs.\n    76→\n    77→The `design-review` workflow validates designs against the spec before planning begins. The existing `review` workflow also checks design-vs-implementation alignment after execution.\n    78→\n    79→open-pencil is integrated as an optional adapter (`open_pencil`) — it is not required for core Wazir functionality.\n    80→\n    81→## Key references\n    82→\n    83→- [Roles & Workflows](roles-and-workflows.md)\n    84→- [Artifact Model](artifact-model.md)\n    85→- [Host Exports](../reference/host-exports.md)\n    86→- [Hooks](../reference/hooks.md)\n    87→- [Expertise & Antipatterns](composition-engine.md)\n    88→"}]},"uuid":"0d2f544c-6eba-4475-a345-8915f4a8f401","timestamp":"2026-03-20T13:41:15.722Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"8b9d328d-f9cf-43f5-9a46-26c153542fed","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir","sessionId":"0c5a9bfa-6816-42b1-a97d-37ae7dad26c5","version":"2.1.80","gitBranch":"feat/remaining-6-fixes","slug":"mighty-wondering-giraffe"}

Let me compile the research findings.\n\n---\n\n# Controller Pattern Research: Agent Framework Source Analysis\n\n## 1. CrewAI's Crew Execution Loop\n\n**Source:** `lib/crewai/src/crewai/crew.py` -- `_execute_tasks()` method (line ~1170)\n\n### The Loop\n\nCrewAI's controller is a simple sequential for-loop inside `_execute_tasks()`:\n\n```python\nfor task_index, task in enumerate(tasks):\n    exec_data, task_outputs, last_sync_output = prepare_task_execution(...)\n    if exec_data.should_skip:\n        continue\n\n    if isinstance(task, ConditionalTask):\n        skipped_task_output = self._handle_conditional_task(...)\n        if skipped_task_output:\n            task_outputs.append(skipped_task_output)\n            continue\n\n    if task.async_execution:\n        context = self._get_context(task, [last_sync_output] if last_sync_output else [])\n        future = task.execute_async(agent=exec_data.agent, context=context, tools=exec_data.tools)\n        futures.append((task, future, task_index))\n    else:\n        if futures:\n            task_outputs = self._process_async_tasks(futures, was_replayed)\n            futures.clear()\n        context = self._get_context(task, task_outputs)\n        task_output = task.execute_sync(agent=exec_data.agent, context=context, tools=exec_data.tools)\n        task_outputs.append(task_output)\n        self._process_task_result(task, task_output)\n```\n\n### Controller Data\n\nThe `Crew` object holds:\n- `self.tasks: list[Task]` -- ordered task list\n- `self.agents: list[BaseAgent]` -- agent pool\n- `self.process: Process` -- sequential or hierarchical\n- `self._memory` -- optional unified memory (shared across agents)\n- `self.execution_logs: list[dict]` -- per-task execution logs\n- `self.usage_metrics` -- token tracking\n\n### Context Passing\n\nContext flows through **two mechanisms**:\n1. **Implicit:** If `task.context` is `NOT_SPECIFIED`, the static method `_get_context()` calls `aggregate_raw_outputs_from_task_outputs(task_outputs)` -- it concatenates ALL previous task raw outputs as a single string.\n2. **Explicit:** If `task.context` is a list of specific Task objects, it calls `aggregate_raw_outputs_from_tasks(task.context)` -- only those tasks' `.output.raw` values are concatenated.\n\nThere is no structured state object. Context is raw string concatenation.\n\n### Failure Handling\n\n- **No retry at the crew level.** If a task's `execute_sync` throws, the exception propagates up through `kickoff()`, which emits `CrewKickoffFailedEvent` and re-raises.\n- **Guardrails** provide per-task validation: a `guardrail` function returns `(bool, Any)`. If it fails, the task retries up to `guardrail_max_retries` (default 3). But this is inside the Task, not the Crew loop.\n- **ConditionalTask** can skip tasks based on the output of previous tasks. The condition is evaluated by `check_conditional_skip()`.\n- **No partial resume.** If the crew fails at task 7 of 10, you restart from scratch (unless using `replay()` which re-starts from a specific task_id using stored outputs).\n\n### Key Insight\n\nCrewAI's controller is **dead simple**: a for-loop with string concatenation for context. The \"intelligence\" is in the agents/tasks, not the controller. Hierarchical mode just injects a manager agent that uses delegation tools, but the loop itself is identical.\n\n---\n\n## 2. LangGraph's prepare_next_tasks\n\n**Source:** `libs/langgraph/langgraph/pregel/_algo.py` -- `prepare_next_tasks()` function, and `_loop.py` -- `PregelLoop.tick()` method.\n\n### The Execution Model\n\nLangGraph follows the **Pregel/Bulk Synchronous Parallel** model with three phases per step:\n\n1. **Plan** (`prepare_next_tasks`): Determine which nodes fire this step\n2. **Execute** (`PregelRunner.tick`): Run all selected nodes in parallel\n3. **Update** (`apply_writes`): Apply all writes to channels atomically\n\nThe outer loop is `PregelLoop.tick()`:\n\n```python\ndef tick(self) -> bool:\n    if self.step > self.stop:\n        self.status = \"out_of_steps\"\n        return False\n\n    self.tasks = prepare_next_tasks(\n        self.checkpoint, self.checkpoint_pending_writes,\n        self.nodes, self.channels, self.managed,\n        self.config, self.step, self.stop,\n        for_execution=True, ...\n    )\n\n    if not self.tasks:\n        self.status = \"done\"\n        return False\n\n    # interrupt_before check\n    # ... execute tasks ...\n    return True\n\ndef after_tick(self):\n    self.updated_channels = apply_writes(\n        self.checkpoint, self.channels,\n        self.tasks.values(), ...\n    )\n    self.checkpoint_pending_writes.clear()\n    self._put_checkpoint({\"source\": \"loop\"})\n    # interrupt_after check\n```\n\n### How prepare_next_tasks Decides What Fires\n\nThe function checks which **channels were updated** in the previous step, then finds nodes whose **triggers** include those channels:\n\n```python\nif updated_channels and trigger_to_nodes:\n    triggered_nodes = set()\n    for channel in updated_channels:\n        if node_ids := trigger_to_nodes.get(channel):\n            triggered_nodes.update(node_ids)\n    candidate_nodes = sorted(triggered_nodes)\n```\n\nFor each candidate, `prepare_single_task()` checks whether the node's trigger channels are actually available (have new values), builds the task input from channel values, and returns a `PregelExecutableTask`.\n\nThere are two task types:\n- **PULL tasks**: Nodes triggered by channel updates (edges)\n- **PUSH tasks**: Explicit `Send` commands (dynamic dispatch to specific nodes)\n\n### Controller Data\n\n`PregelLoop` holds:\n- `self.channels: Mapping[str, BaseChannel]` -- typed communication channels\n- `self.checkpoint: Checkpoint` -- versioned state snapshot (channel_versions, versions_seen)\n- `self.nodes: Mapping[str, PregelNode]` -- the graph's node definitions\n- `self.tasks: dict[str, PregelExecutableTask]` -- current step's executable tasks\n- `self.updated_channels: set[str]` -- channels modified in last step\n- `self.trigger_to_nodes: Mapping[str, Sequence[str]]` -- edge lookup table\n\n### Context Passing\n\nContext passes through **typed channels**, not raw strings:\n- `LastValue(type)` -- stores the last value written (like state fields)\n- `Topic(type)` -- accumulates multiple values (pub/sub)\n- `BinaryOperatorAggregate(type, op)` -- reduces values with a binary operator\n\nNodes read from subscribed channels and write to output channels. Writes are invisible until the next step (BSP isolation).\n\n### Failure Handling\n\n- **RetryPolicy**: Configurable per-node with `max_attempts`, `initial_interval`, `backoff_factor`, `jitter`. The `run_with_retry()` function in `_retry.py` handles exponential backoff.\n- **Checkpointing**: Every step saves a checkpoint. On failure, execution can resume from the last checkpoint. The `_put_checkpoint()` method persists state, channel versions, and pending writes.\n- **GraphInterrupt**: Nodes can interrupt execution (human-in-the-loop). The graph can be resumed with `Command(resume=...)`.\n\n### Key Insight\n\nLangGraph's controller is **data-driven**: channel updates determine what fires next. It is the most sophisticated of the four -- full checkpointing, retry policies, typed channels, and BSP isolation. But it is designed for graph topologies, not linear phase pipelines.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Superpowers' Subagent-Driven Development\n\n**Source:** `obra/amplifier-bundle-superpowers` -- `recipes/subagent-development.yaml` and `modes/execute-plan.md` (from `bkrabach/superpowers`)\n\n### The Architecture\n\nSuperpowers does NOT have a programmatic controller. The controller IS the LLM itself, operating under strict behavioral constraints defined in `execute-plan.md`:\n\n> \"YOU DO NOT WRITE CODE IN THIS MODE. YOU DO NOT EDIT FILES. YOU DO NOT IMPLEMENT ANYTHING DIRECTLY. Your ONLY job is to dispatch subagents and track their progress. You are a conductor, not a musician.\"\n\n### The Fixed Sequence (Per Task)\n\nThe state machine is explicitly defined:\n\n```\nLOAD PLAN\n  -> Read plan, create todo list\n\nFOR EACH TASK:\n  -> DELEGATE implementer\n     -> Wait for completion\n  -> DELEGATE spec-reviewer\n     -> PASS? Continue\n     -> FAIL? DELEGATE implementer fix\n  -> DELEGATE code-quality-reviewer\n     -> PASS? Next task\n     -> FAIL? DELEGATE implementer fix\n  -> Mark task complete in todos\n\nALL TASKS DONE\n  -> Summary of commits and results\n```\n\n### Controller Data\n\nThe controller holds context in **recipe variables** (`{{tasks}}`, `{{task_implementations}}`, `{{spec_reviews}}`, `{{quality_reviews}}`). Each stage's `output:` field names a variable that becomes available to subsequent stages via `{{variable_name}}` interpolation.\n\nThe recipe YAML has:\n- `stages:` -- ordered execution stages\n- `steps:` per stage -- ordered steps within a stage\n- `foreach:` -- iteration over collections\n- `collect:` -- accumulates outputs from foreach iterations\n- `approval:` -- human gates between stages\n\n### Context Passing Between Agents\n\nEach subagent gets a **crafted prompt** with ONLY the context it needs:\n- Implementer: task spec + project conventions + TDD instructions\n- Spec reviewer: implementation output + original spec\n- Quality reviewer: spec review results + implementation output\n\nCritical rule: **\"Never pass session history to subagents; craft focused prompts.\"** Each subagent is fresh -- no context pollution.\n\n### Failure Handling\n\n- **Implementer statuses**: DONE, DONE_WITH_CONCERNS, NEEDS_CONTEXT, BLOCKED\n- **Review loop**: If spec-reviewer returns FAIL, delegate back to implementer with fix instructions. Repeat until PASS.\n- **Escalation**: BLOCKED status gets assessed -- unimplemented dependency gets reordered, design conflicts escalate to user, environment bugs trigger systematic-debugging skill.\n- **Human gate**: After all tasks, a mandatory approval gate (`approval.required: true`) blocks automatic merge.\n\n### Key Insight\n\nSuperpowers proves that the LLM-as-controller pattern works. The controller is the orchestrating agent, constrained by mode instructions to ONLY delegate. Fresh context per subagent is the critical design choice -- it prevents context pollution and enables focused attention. The `foreach` + `collect` pattern in the recipe YAML is the iteration mechanism.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Framework Comparison Table\n\n| Dimension | CrewAI | LangGraph | Superpowers |\n|-----------|--------|-----------|-------------|\n| **Controller** | Python for-loop | BSP tick loop | LLM-as-orchestrator + YAML recipe |\n| **State** | `list[TaskOutput]` (strings) | Typed channels + checkpoint | Recipe variables (`{{var}}`) |\n| **Context passing** | String concatenation of all prior outputs | Channel reads (typed, versioned) | Crafted per-agent prompts (no history) |\n| **Failure handling** | Exception propagates, no retry | RetryPolicy + checkpoint resume | Status codes (DONE/BLOCKED) + review loop |\n| **Partial resume** | `replay(task_id)` from stored outputs | Checkpoint-based resume | Re-run recipe from stage |\n| **Parallelism** | `async_execution` flag on tasks | All triggered nodes run in parallel | Serial only (\"never dispatch in parallel\") |\n| **Human gates** | `human_input` flag on tasks | `interrupt_before`/`interrupt_after` | `approval.required: true` between stages |\n\n---\n\n## 5. Can Claude Code's Agent Tool Be a Controller?\n\n### What the Agent Tool Provides\n\nThe Agent tool spawns a subagent that:\n- Gets its own conversation context (fresh, no pollution)\n- Has access to the same tools (Read, Edit, Bash, Grep, etc.)\n- Returns a text result to the calling agent\n- Runs to completion before the caller proceeds\n\nThis maps directly to the Superpowers pattern: the calling agent IS the controller, the Agent tool IS the `delegate()` call.\n\n### What Works\n\n1. **Sequential dispatch**: Call Agent for phase 1, get result, validate, call Agent for phase 2. This is the CrewAI for-loop pattern.\n2. **Fresh context per phase**: Each Agent call starts clean. This is the Superpowers \"fresh subagent\" principle.\n3. **Crafted prompts**: The controller composes the prompt with exactly the context the subagent needs.\n4. **Validation between phases**: The controller can inspect the Agent's output, run `wazir validate`, check artifacts, and decide whether to proceed or retry.\n\n### What Does NOT Work\n\n1. **No programmatic loop**: The controller is an LLM, not a Python for-loop. It must be instructed to iterate. This is the Superpowers constraint, not a limitation.\n2. **No checkpoint/resume**: If the controller agent dies mid-pipeline, there is no automatic resume. The run state in `~/.wazir/projects/<slug>/` must serve this role.\n3. **No parallel execution**: Agent calls are blocking. No equivalent to CrewAI's `async_execution` or LangGraph's parallel node execution.\n4. **Context window pressure**: The controller accumulates subagent outputs in its own context. Long pipelines with large outputs could exhaust the window.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Concrete Controller Architecture for Wazir\n\n### Design: Controller-as-Role with Agent Tool Dispatch\n\nThe controller is NOT a new component -- it is a **workflow instruction** that tells the host agent to operate as an orchestrator, using the Agent tool for phase dispatch.\n\n### State Schema\n\nThe controller reads and writes run state in `~/.wazir/projects/<slug>/runs/<run-id>/`:\n\n```\nstate.json          # phase progression, status, timestamps\nphase-outputs/      # one file per phase output (keeps it out of context)\n  clarify.md\n  specify.md\n  plan.md\n  execute.md\n  verify.md\n  review.md\nartifacts/          # canonical artifacts (spec, plan, etc.)\n```\n\n`state.json` structure:\n```json\n{\n  \"run_id\": \"run-20260320-...\",\n  \"current_phase\": \"execute\",\n  \"phases\": {\n    \"clarify\":  { \"status\": \"completed\", \"exit_time\": \"...\", \"output_path\": \"phase-outputs/clarify.md\" },\n    \"specify\":  { \"status\": \"completed\", \"exit_time\": \"...\", \"output_path\": \"phase-outputs/specify.md\" },\n    \"plan\":     { \"status\": \"completed\", \"exit_time\": \"...\", \"output_path\": \"phase-outputs/plan.md\" },\n    \"execute\":  { \"status\": \"in_progress\", \"enter_time\": \"...\" },\n    \"verify\":   { \"status\": \"pending\" },\n    \"review\":   { \"status\": \"pending\" }\n  },\n  \"retry_counts\": { \"execute\": 1 },\n  \"gate_approvals\": { \"clarify\": true, \"plan\": true }\n}\n```\n\n### Controller Loop (Pseudocode for the Orchestrating Agent)\n\n```\n1. Read state.json to find current_phase\n2. Check phase_prerequisites from wazir.manifest.yaml\n3. For the next pending phase:\n   a. Read the role contract (roles/<role>.md)\n   b. Read the workflow contract (workflows/<phase>.md)\n   c. Compose the subagent prompt:\n      - Role contract\n      - Workflow instructions\n      - Previous phase output (read from file, not from context)\n      - Required artifacts list\n   d. Dispatch via Agent tool\n   e. Capture output to phase-outputs/<phase>.md\n   f. Validate:\n      - Required artifacts exist\n      - wazir validate manifest passes\n      - Phase-specific checks (tests pass for execute, etc.)\n   g. If valid: update state.json, advance to next phase\n   h. If invalid: retry (up to max_retries), then escalate to user\n4. After all phases complete: run final review as a separate Agent call\n```\n\n### Prompt Template for Subagent Dispatch\n\n```markdown\nYou are the {role_name} for Wazir run {run_id}.\n\n## Your Role Contract\n{content of roles/<role>.md}\n\n## Workflow Instructions  \n{content of workflows/<phase>.md}\n\n## Input From Previous Phase\n{content of phase-outputs/<previous_phase>.md -- read from file, NOT from controller context}\n\n## Required Outputs\nYou must produce these artifacts:\n{list from phase_prerequisites for the NEXT phase}\n\n## Constraints\n- Stay within the scope defined in the workflow\n- Write artifacts to the designated paths\n- Report your status at completion: DONE | BLOCKED <reason> | NEEDS_INPUT <question>\n```\n\n### Context Window Management (Solving the Accumulation Problem)\n\nThe critical lesson from Superpowers: **never pass session history to subagents**. For Wazir:\n\n1. **File-mediated context**: Phase outputs are written to `phase-outputs/`. The controller reads the file path, not the content. The subagent reads the file directly.\n2. **Summarized handoffs**: For phases that produce large output (execute can produce hundreds of lines of code changes), the controller passes a **summary** to the next subagent, not the raw output. The subagent can read full files if needed.\n3. **Controller context budget**: The controller itself holds only: state.json (~200 tokens), phase status lines (~50 tokens each), and the current subagent's result summary (~500 tokens). Total controller overhead: ~1,500 tokens for a 6-phase pipeline.\n\n### Failure Handling Matrix\n\n| Subagent Status | Controller Action |\n|----------------|-------------------|\n| DONE | Validate artifacts, advance to next phase |\n| DONE_WITH_CONCERNS | Read concerns, decide: retry or accept with note |\n| NEEDS_INPUT | Route question to user via `wazir capture question` |\n| BLOCKED | Log blocker, escalate to user, do NOT auto-retry |\n| Exception/timeout | Retry up to `max_retries` (default 2), then escalate |\n| Validation failure | Re-dispatch subagent with failure details appended to prompt |\n\n### What This Architecture Gives Wazir\n\n1. **Phase isolation**: Each phase runs in a fresh Agent context. No context pollution between clarifier and executor.\n2. **Checkpoint/resume**: `state.json` records phase progression. If the session dies, the next session reads state.json and picks up from the last completed phase.\n3. **Validation gates**: Between every phase, the controller validates artifacts and can block advancement. This is the LangGraph `interrupt_before` equivalent.\n4. **Review loops**: Per-task review within the execute phase uses nested Agent calls: dispatch implementer, dispatch reviewer, loop until approved. This is the Superpowers two-stage review pattern.\n5. **Host portability**: The controller is prompt-driven, not code-driven. It works in Claude Code, Codex, Gemini CLI, or Cursor -- all of which support some form of subagent dispatch.\n\n### Architecture Diagram\n\n```\n                    ┌─────────────────────┐\n                    │  Controller Agent    │\n                    │  (host LLM session)  │\n                    │                      │\n                    │  Reads: state.json   │\n                    │  Reads: manifest     │\n                    │  Reads: role/workflow │\n                    └──────────┬──────────┘\n                               │\n            ┌──────────────────┼──────────────────┐\n            │ Agent tool call  │ Agent tool call   │ ...\n            ▼                  ▼                   ▼\n    ┌──────────────┐  ┌──────────────┐  ┌──────────────┐\n    │  Clarifier   │  │  Executor    │  │  Reviewer    │\n    │  (subagent)  │  │  (subagent)  │  │  (subagent)  │\n    │              │  │              │  │              │\n    │  Fresh ctx   │  │  Fresh ctx   │  │  Fresh ctx   │\n    │  Role prompt │  │  Role prompt │  │  Role prompt │\n    │  Prev output │  │  Prev output │  │  Prev output │\n    └──────┬───────┘  └──────┬───────┘  └──────┬───────┘\n           │                 │                  │\n           ▼                 ▼                  ▼\n    phase-outputs/     phase-outputs/     phase-outputs/\n    clarify.md         execute.md         review.md\n           │                 │                  │\n           └────────┬────────┘──────────────────┘\n                    ▼\n              state.json\n              (phase progression)\n```\n\n### Comparison to Alternatives\n\nWhy this over a Python/TypeScript controller (like CrewAI or LangGraph):\n\n- **No runtime dependency**: Wazir ships as prompt files, not as a package to install. The controller runs inside the host LLM, not alongside it.\n- **Host portability**: Works in any host that supports subagent dispatch (Claude Agent tool, Codex `codex exec`, Gemini tool-use, Cursor agent mode).\n- **Simpler failure model**: No process management, no async coordination, no channel type system. Just: dispatch, validate, advance.\n\nWhy this over raw Superpowers-style mode instructions:\n\n- **Persistent state**: `state.json` enables resume across sessions. Superpowers' recipe YAML has no persistence.\n- **Manifest-driven prerequisites**: Phase gates come from `wazir.manifest.yaml`, not hardcoded in prompts. Adding a new phase is a manifest change, not a prompt rewrite.\n- **Validation hooks**: `wazir validate` provides programmatic validation between phases, not just LLM judgment."}],"stop_reason":"end_turn","stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":3,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1275,"cache_read_input_tokens":84622,"output_tokens":5515,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":1275},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"}},"requestId":"req_011CZERnWqWjgxXonJV2tJo8","type":"assistant","uuid":"4dcbc784-bbdd-4a1b-944b-d37be7e765a1","timestamp":"2026-03-20T13:43:29.536Z","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir","sessionId":"0c5a9bfa-6816-42b1-a97d-37ae7dad26c5","version":"2.1.80","gitBranch":"feat/remaining-6-fixes","slug":"mighty-wondering-giraffe"}
